{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016cZzzkzkCWfAVMpsiqeeZM","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01TTPgk6kVvSD9QgGdHPjMid","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy Connection Pool Management Troubleshooting Runbook\n\n## 1. Architecture Overview\n\n### Connection Pool Organization\n\nEnvoy's connection pools are the critical infrastructure layer managing upstream connections. Understanding their architecture is essential for diagnosing production issues.\n\n#### Pool Hierarchy\n\n- **Per-Cluster Pools**: Each upstream cluster has its own pool manager\n- **Per-Host Pools**: Within each cluster, a separate connection pool exists for each upstream host\n- **Per-Thread Pools**: Connection pools are NOT shared across worker threads—each thread maintains its own independent pools\n- **Per-Priority Pools**: Separate capacity tracking for DEFAULT and HIGH priority streams (separate circuit breaker limits)\n\n#### Connection State Machine\n\nEach connection progresses through well-defined states:\n\n```\nConnecting → Ready/ReadyForEarlyData → Busy → Draining → Closed\n```\n\n**State Definitions:**\n\n- **Connecting**: Connection is being established, not yet available for requests\n  - File: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:90`\n  - Timer active: `connect_timeout` (default varies by cluster)\n\n- **Ready**: Connection is established, has capacity for additional concurrent streams\n  - HTTP/2: Has unused concurrent stream slots\n  - HTTP/1.1: Only one stream active at a time\n  - Transitions to Busy when capacity is exhausted\n\n- **ReadyForEarlyData** (HTTP/3 only): Connection established but handshake in progress\n  - Can accept requests before full TLS handshake\n  - Transitions to Ready or Busy on handshake completion\n\n- **Busy**: Connection is at its concurrent stream limit\n  - No new streams can be attached\n  - Pending requests queue and wait for capacity\n  - Transitions to Ready when a stream completes\n  - File: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:256-258`\n\n- **Draining**: No new streams will be assigned; connection closes after active streams complete\n  - Triggered by:\n    - HTTP/2 GOAWAY from peer\n    - Connection reaching `max_requests_per_connection` limit\n    - Administrative drain command\n  - File: `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`\n\n- **Closed**: Connection is no longer usable, queued for destruction\n  - Scheduled for deferred deletion\n  - All stream state has been released\n\n#### Internal Tracking Structures\n\nThe pool maintains several lists:\n\n```cpp\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> ready_clients_;              // Connections in Ready state\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> busy_clients_;               // Connections in Busy state\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> connecting_clients_;         // Connections in Connecting state\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> early_data_clients_;         // Connections in ReadyForEarlyData state\nstd::list<PendingStreamPtr> pending_streams_;           // Queued requests waiting for connections\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:300+`\n\n#### Capacity Tracking\n\nThe pool tracks available stream capacity across all connections:\n\n- `connecting_stream_capacity_`: Potential capacity from in-flight connections\n- `connecting_and_connected_stream_capacity_`: Total potential capacity (connecting + ready + busy)\n- `num_active_streams_`: Currently active request streams\n\nThese values are critical for:\n- Determining if new requests should be queued or rejected\n- Deciding whether to preconnect\n- Enforcing circuit breaker limits\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:26-50`\n\n### HTTP Protocol Differences\n\n#### HTTP/1.1 Pools\n- **Max concurrent streams per connection**: 1 (strictly enforced)\n- **Connection lifecycle**: Long-lived or short-lived based on `keep-alive`\n- **Queue behavior**: Pending requests queue when all connections are at capacity\n- **File**: `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.cc`\n\n#### HTTP/2 Pools\n- **Max concurrent streams per connection**: Configurable, negotiated via SETTINGS frame\n- **Default limit**: 2^29 (effectively unlimited in most cases)\n- **SETTINGS negotiation**: Server can lower max streams dynamically\n- **Stream multiplexing**: Multiple requests share one TCP connection\n- **Handling GOAWAY**: Transitions connection to Draining state, opens new connections for pending requests\n- **File**: `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.cc`\n\n#### HTTP/3 Pools (QUIC)\n- **Early data**: Requests can be sent before TLS handshake completes (0-RTT)\n- **State**: ReadyForEarlyData is unique to HTTP/3\n- **Connection migration**: Supported by QUIC (not managed by connection pool)\n- **File**: `source/common/http/http3/conn_pool.cc`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Common Failure Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Connection Pool Exhaustion — Pending Requests Overflow\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Upstream requests fail with `PoolFailureReason::Overflow`\n- Admin API shows non-zero `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` metric\n- Client observes 503 responses or request timeouts\n- Logs contain: `\"max pending streams overflow\"` or `\"max pending requests overflow\"`\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe pending request queue has hit the circuit breaker limit. When a new request arrives and there are no ready connections to serve it, the pool attempts to queue it as a pending request. However, the circuit breaker enforces `max_pending_requests` limit per priority level, and additional requests are rejected.\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()\n  → resourceManager(priority_).pendingRequests().canCreate()  [FAILS]\n  → onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason::Overflow)\n  → upstream_rq_pending_overflow_.inc()\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:347-352`\n\n**Why It Happens**:\n1. All connections in the pool are in Busy state (at concurrent stream limit)\n2. New connections are not being created fast enough\n3. Pending request backlog grows, hits `max_pending_requests` limit (default 1024)\n4. Circuit breaker rejects further pending requests\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Check pool statistics via admin API**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -A5 \"upstream_rq_pending\"\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -A5 \"upstream_cx\"\n   ```\n\n   Key metrics:\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_active`: Current pending request count\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_overflow`: Total overflow rejections\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_total`: Cumulative pending requests processed\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_total`: Total connections created\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_active`: Currently active connections\n\n2. **Examine cluster configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.@type | contains(\"Cluster\")) | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\")'\n   ```\n\n   Look for:\n   - `circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_pending_requests`\n   - `circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_connections`\n   - `circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_requests`\n\n3. **Check Envoy logs for connection creation patterns**:\n   ```bash\n   # Enable trace logging for connection pool\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?pool=trace\n\n   # Look for patterns in logs\n   grep \"queueing stream\\|using existing\\|creating new connection\\|max pending\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n4. **Analyze upstream health**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters | grep your_cluster -A20\n   ```\n   - Are all hosts up? If hosts are down or slow, connection creation fails\n   - Check `cx_total`, `rq_total`, and response times\n\n5. **Review request patterns**:\n   - Are requests slower than expected?\n   - Is the arrival rate higher than normal?\n   - Are requests getting retried (increasing pending queue)?\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Increase `max_pending_requests`** (short-term):\n   ```yaml\n   cluster_managers:\n     cluster:\n       name: your_cluster\n       circuit_breakers:\n         thresholds:\n         - priority: DEFAULT\n           max_pending_requests: 2048  # Increase from default 1024\n   ```\n   **Caveat**: This masks the root cause; investigate why pending backlog grows\n\n2. **Increase `max_connections`** to handle more concurrent work:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 2048  # Increase from default 1024\n   ```\n\n3. **Increase `max_requests`** per priority:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_requests: 2048  # Increase from default 1024\n   ```\n\n4. **Improve upstream responsiveness** (long-term):\n   - Optimize upstream service latency\n   - Add upstream capacity (more instances/hosts)\n   - Configure connection pooling on upstream side\n   - Enable request pipelining (HTTP/2 multiplexing)\n\n5. **Lower request timeout** if acceptable:\n   - Prevents slow requests from holding connections\n   - Frees capacity sooner for other requests\n\n**Code References**:\n- Pool overflow check: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:347`\n- Pending overflow metric: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:351`\n- Resource manager (circuit breaker enforcement): `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.cc`\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 2: Upstream Connection Reset or Premature Close\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Sporadic `LocalClose` or `RemoteClose` events in logs\n- Non-zero `upstream_cx_connect_fail` or `upstream_cx_reset` metrics\n- Requests fail mid-stream or don't reach upstream at all\n- Error messages: `\"upstream connection reset\"`, `\"connection refused\"`\n- `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` increases (pending requests fail)\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe upstream server is actively closing connections before streams complete. This can be due to:\n1. Upstream resource exhaustion (out of memory, CPU spike)\n2. Upstream graceful shutdown (sending GOAWAY or closing connections)\n3. Network issues (packet loss, timeout)\n4. Upstream load balancer killing idle connections\n5. Firewall/NAT timeout closing long-lived connections\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nNetwork::ConnectionCallbacks::onEvent(ConnectionEvent::RemoteClose)\n  → ConnPoolImplBase::onConnectionEvent()\n  → [If active streams exist]\n    → onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason::RemoteReset)\n    → upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject_.inc()\n  → [If idle, just clean up]\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:552-670`\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Isolate the failure pattern**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_reset|upstream_cx_destroy|upstream_cx_connect_fail\"\n   ```\n\n   - `upstream_cx_reset`: Unexpected disconnects\n   - `upstream_cx_connect_fail`: Connection failures during establishment\n   - `upstream_cx_destroy_local`: Local side closed (normal, drained)\n   - `upstream_cx_destroy_remote`: Remote side closed (abnormal)\n\n2. **Check per-host statistics**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters/your_cluster/stats\n   ```\n   - Are failures concentrated on one host? (indicates that host is unhealthy)\n   - Are they evenly distributed? (indicates network or upstream cluster issue)\n\n3. **Review Envoy logs for connection events**:\n   ```bash\n   # Enable debug logging\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?pool=debug\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?connection=debug\n\n   # Search for close events\n   grep \"ConnectionEvent::\\|RemoteClose\\|LocalClose\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n4. **Check upstream service health**:\n   ```bash\n   # Monitor upstream response times\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_rq_time_bucket|upstream_rq_pending_active\"\n\n   # Check if upstream is slow or unresponsive\n   # Look for increasing request latency\n   ```\n\n5. **Examine access logs for failed requests**:\n   ```bash\n   # Look for upstream_transport_failure_reason\n   grep \"upstream_transport_failure_reason\" access.log\n   grep \"upstream_connection_failure\" access.log\n   ```\n\n6. **Test connectivity to upstream**:\n   ```bash\n   # From Envoy pod/container:\n   telnet upstream-host upstream-port\n   timeout 5 bash -c 'cat < /dev/null > /dev/tcp/upstream-host/port'\n   ```\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Increase `connect_timeout`** if connections are dropping during establishment:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster:\n     name: your_cluster\n     connect_timeout: 5s  # Increase from default 1s\n   ```\n\n2. **Configure `tcp_keepalive`** to detect dead connections:\n   ```yaml\n   upstream_connection_options:\n     tcp_keepalive:\n       keepalive_probes: 3\n       keepalive_interval: 10s\n       keepalive_time: 30s\n   ```\n\n3. **Enable health checking** to detect unhealthy hosts:\n   ```yaml\n   health_checks:\n   - timeout: 1s\n     interval: 10s\n     unhealthy_threshold: 3\n     healthy_threshold: 2\n     http_health_check:\n       path: /health\n   ```\n\n4. **Set `idle_timeout`** to proactively close and recreate idle connections:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster_connection_draining:\n     idle_timeout: 300s\n   ```\n\n5. **Increase `max_requests_per_connection`** (HTTP/1.1) to reduce connection recycling:\n   ```yaml\n   http_protocol_options:\n     max_requests_per_connection: 10000\n   ```\n\n6. **Add connection draining grace period**:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster:\n     drain_connections_on_host_removal: true\n   ```\n\n**Fix - Operational/Upstream Changes**:\n- Optimize upstream service to handle load better\n- Add more upstream capacity\n- Review upstream garbage collection and resource limits\n- Ensure upstream keep-alive settings match Envoy expectations\n- Disable aggressive TCP timeouts on load balancers\n\n**Code References**:\n- Connection event handler: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:552`\n- Remote close handling: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:555-585`\n- TCP connection creation: `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc:14-35`\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 3: Circuit Breaker Triggering Unexpectedly\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Admin stats show `upstream_cx_overflow` or `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` increasing\n- All requests to a cluster start failing with \"overflow\" error\n- No actual errors on upstream; capacity appears available\n- Happens suddenly after a spike in traffic\n- Request errors after other clusters' traffic spikes\n\n**Root Cause**:\nCircuit breaker limits are being hit even though the upstream appears healthy. Common causes:\n1. **Shared circuit breaker limits**: Multiple clusters or priorities share resource manager\n2. **Capacity miscalculation**: `max_connections` or `max_pending_requests` set too low for actual concurrency\n3. **Slow response times**: Connections held longer, capacity exhausted sooner\n4. **Uneven load distribution**: Load balancer concentrating traffic on few hosts\n5. **Rate limiting**: Upstream rate limiting causes queue buildup\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nConnPoolImplBase::tryCreateNewConnection()\n  → host_->canCreateConnection(priority_)  [Circuit breaker check]\n  → [If exceeded]: upstream_cx_overflow_.inc()\n  → return ConnectionResult::NoConnectionRateLimited\n\nOR\n\nConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()\n  → resourceManager(priority_).pendingRequests().canCreate()\n  → [If exceeded]: upstream_rq_pending_overflow_.inc()\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:198-202`, `347-352`\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Check circuit breaker limits vs actual load**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.@type | contains(\"Cluster\")) | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\") | .cluster.circuit_breakers'\n   ```\n\n   Compare configured limits with:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_active|upstream_rq_active|upstream_rq_pending_active\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Check for cascading failures**:\n   ```bash\n   # Get stats for multiple clusters\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_overflow|upstream_rq_pending_overflow\"\n\n   # If multiple clusters overflow at same time, check cluster manager limits\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"cluster_manager\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Review request latency**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"upstream_rq_time\"\n\n   # If latencies are high, connections are held longer\n   # Check if upstream is slow\n   ```\n\n4. **Examine resource manager state**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -A3 \"cluster.your_cluster.resource_manager\"\n   ```\n\n5. **Check priority-based limits**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"circuit_breakers\"\n   ```\n   - DEFAULT priority requests may be exhausted\n   - HIGH priority may have separate limits\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Adjust `max_connections` based on realistic concurrency**:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 4096  # Increase based on observed peak\n   ```\n\n2. **Adjust `max_requests` based on actual concurrent streams**:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_requests: 4096\n   ```\n\n3. **Use per-host limits** to distribute load more fairly:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 512\n     per_host_thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 50  # Limit per individual host\n   ```\n\n4. **Set separate limits for HIGH priority**:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_requests: 4096\n     - priority: HIGH\n       max_requests: 512  # Reserve capacity for critical traffic\n   ```\n\n5. **Monitor and increase limits based on metrics**:\n   - Set `track_remaining: true` to expose remaining capacity\n   - Create alerts on `circuit_breakers.*.remaining` metrics\n   - Incrementally increase limits based on observed peak\n\n**Code References**:\n- Circuit breaker enforcement: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:198-202`\n- Resource manager (limits enforcement): `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.h`\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 4: HTTP/2 GOAWAY Causing Request Failures\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Sporadic request failures after sustained traffic\n- Logs contain `\"remote goaway\"` messages\n- Admin stats show `upstream_cx_close_notify` incrementing\n- Multiple connection resets immediately after GOAWAY\n- Cascading failures as pending requests fail\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe upstream HTTP/2 server sent a GOAWAY frame, signaling that it will not accept new streams on this connection. Envoy must:\n1. Stop sending new streams to this connection\n2. Drain existing streams\n3. Open new connections for pending/future requests\n4. If upstream is not opening new connections, pending requests accumulate and fail\n\nGOAWAY can be initiated by:\n- Upstream graceful shutdown\n- Upstream resource exhaustion\n- Upstream hitting stream/connection limits\n- Upstream configured to close connections periodically\n- Load balancer injecting connection resets\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nHttp::MultiplexedActiveClientBase::onGoAway()\n  → upstream_cx_close_notify_.inc()\n  → [If state != Draining]:\n    → [If no active streams]: close()\n    → [Else]: transitionActiveClientState(Draining)\n  → scheduleOnUpstreamReady()  [Attach pending streams to new connections]\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Confirm GOAWAY events**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_close_notify\n   ```\n   - Non-zero value indicates GOAWAY was received\n   - Increasing value indicates repeated GOAWAY events\n\n2. **Check connection state transitions**:\n   ```bash\n   # Enable trace logging\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?http=trace\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?pool=debug\n\n   grep -E \"remote goaway|transitionActiveClientState.*Draining\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n3. **Examine request failure patterns**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"upstream_rq_reset\\|upstream_rq_failed\"\n\n   # Correlate with GOAWAY events in timestamps\n   ```\n\n4. **Check if upstream can accept new connections**:\n   ```bash\n   # From Envoy:\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters/your_cluster | grep cx_\n\n   # Look for:\n   # - Increasing cx_total (new connections opened after GOAWAY)\n   # - Stuck cx_active (connections not draining)\n   ```\n\n5. **Review upstream logs**:\n   - Is upstream gracefully shutting down?\n   - Are connection limits being hit?\n   - Are resource limits triggering shutdown?\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Increase `max_requests_per_connection`** to reduce GOAWAY frequency:\n   ```yaml\n   http_protocol_options:\n     max_requests_per_connection: 100000  # Increase from default (often 1024)\n   ```\n\n2. **Enable preconnection** to have connections ready when GOAWAY occurs:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster:\n     name: your_cluster\n     preconnect_policy:\n       per_upstream_preconnect_ratio: 1.5  # Open 150% of needed connections\n   ```\n\n3. **Increase connection pool size** to absorb GOAWAY events:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 8192\n   ```\n\n4. **Configure read buffer limits** to prevent buffer exhaustion during GOAWAY:\n   ```yaml\n   http_protocol_options:\n     per_connection_buffer_limit_bytes: 32768\n   ```\n\n5. **Add connection draining timeout**:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster_connection_draining:\n     drain_timeout: 5s\n   ```\n\n**Fix - Operational/Upstream Changes**:\n- Review upstream connection/stream limits\n- Ensure upstream has enough capacity to handle load\n- Configure upstream to send GOAWAY less frequently (if possible)\n- Implement graceful shutdown with longer drain periods upstream\n- Use connection pooling on upstream side\n\n**Code References**:\n- GOAWAY handler: `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`\n- Connection draining: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:304-306`\n- Preconnect policy: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:92-157`\n\n---\n\n## 3. in pool | Non-zero = pool backpressure |\n| `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` | Counter | Pending requests rejected | Non-zero = requests dropped due to queue full |\n| `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` | Counter | Pending requests failed due to connection reset | Indicates upstream instability |\n| `upstream_rq_time` | Histogram | Request latency (ms) | High values = slow upstream |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Configuration Fixes and Tuning\n\n### Circuit Breaker Configuration\n\nCircuit breakers prevent resource exhaustion by enforcing hard limits on concurrent connections, requests, and pending requests.\n\n#### Default Limits\n\n```yaml\ncircuit_breakers:\n  thresholds:\n  - priority: DEFAULT\n    max_connections: 1024\n    max_pending_requests: 1024\n    max_requests: 1024\n    max_retries: 3\n```\n\n#### Tuning Strategy\n\n1. **Baseline**: Start with defaults\n2. **Measure**: Observe peak values of `upstream_cx_active`, `upstream_rq_active`, `upstream_rq_pending_active`\n3. **Calculate**: Set limits to 1.5-2x peak observed values\n4. **Monitor**: Watch for `*_overflow` metrics; increase if frequently triggered\n5. **Iterate**: Gradually tune based on production behavior\n\n#### Configuration Template\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  # Circuit breaker limits\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n    - priority: DEFAULT\n      # Maximum simultaneous connections to cluster\n      # Tune: Observe upstream_cx_active, set to ~1.5x peak\n      max_connections: 512\n\n      # Maximum pending requests in pool queue\n      # Tune: Observe upstream_rq_pending_active, set to ~1.5x peak\n      max_pending_requests: 512\n\n      # Maximum simultaneous requests\n      # Tune: Observe upstream_rq_active, set to ~1.5x peak\n      max_requests: 512\n\n      # Maximum retries in flight\n      # Increase if retry storms occur\n      max_retries: 3\n\n      # (Optional) Per-host limits to distribute load evenly\n      # Only max_connections is supported per-host\n      max_connection_pools: 256\n\n    # (Optional) Separate limits for HIGH priority traffic\n    - priority: HIGH\n      max_connections: 256\n      max_pending_requests: 256\n      max_requests: 256\n\n    # (Optional) Per-host limits\n    per_host_thresholds:\n    - priority: DEFAULT\n      max_connections: 64  # Limit per individual host\n```\n\n### HTTP Connection Pool Configuration\n\n#### HTTP/1.1 Pools\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: http1_cluster\n  protocol: HTTP\n\n  http_protocol_options:\n    # Max requests per connection before recycling\n    # Tune: Higher = fewer connections, lower = better isolation\n    max_requests_per_connection: 10000\n\n    # TCP keep-alive settings\n    upstream_connection_options:\n      tcp_keepalive:\n        keepalive_probes: 3\n        keepalive_interval: 10s\n        keepalive_time: 30s\n```\n\n#### HTTP/2 Pools\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: http2_cluster\n  protocol: HTTP2\n\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    # Max concurrent streams per connection\n    # Tune: Higher = better multiplexing, lower = more connections\n    max_concurrent_streams: 100\n\n    # Connection idleness timeout\n    # Tune: Higher = long-lived connections, lower = connection recycle\n    idle_timeout: 600s\n\n  # HTTP/2-specific settings\n  http_protocol_options:\n    # Keep-alive period to prevent proxy timeouts\n    idle_timeout: 600s\n```\n\n#### Connection Timeout Configuration\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  # Timeout for establishing upstream connection\n  # Tune: Increase if upstream is geographically distant or slow\n  connect_timeout: 5s  # Default: 1s\n```\n\n### Preconnection Policy\n\nPreconnection improves latency by opening connections before requests arrive.\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  preconnect_policy:\n    # Ratio of connections to open speculatively\n    # Example: 1.5 = open 1.5x as many connections as active requests\n    per_upstream_preconnect_ratio: 1.5\n```\n\n### Connection Draining Configuration\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  # Drain timeout when removing cluster\n  cluster_connection_draining:\n    drain_timeout: 5s\n\n  # Close connections when removing host from cluster\n  close_connections_on_host_removal: true\n```\n\n### Resource Manager (Global Limits)\n\nEnvoy has global limits that apply across all clusters. If multiple clusters compete for resources, global limits may be exceeded first.\n\nCheck global limits via admin API:\n\n```bash\ncurl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"cluster_manager|resource_manager\"\n```\n\nOverride via bootstrap config (requires restart):\n\n```yaml\nbootstrap:\n  overload_manager:\n    refresh_interval: 0.25s\n    actions:\n    - name: envoy.overload_actions.shrink_heap\n      triggers:\n      - name: envoy.resource_monitors.fixed_heap\n        scaled: true\n        trigger_threshold: 0.9\n\n    # Connection limits\n    resource_limits:\n    - name: rpc.downstream_rq_active\n      actions:\n      - name: envoy.load_shed_points.http_connection_manager_decode_headers\n        action: SCALE_TIMER_MIN_WAIT\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Summary and Best Practices\n\n### Quick Troubleshooting Checklist\n\n1. **Identify the failure**:\n   - Check `/stats` for `*_overflow`, `*_reset`, `*_fail`, `*_close_notify` metrics\n   - Look at timestamps to correlate with traffic spikes or changes\n\n2. **Check configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\") | .cluster.circuit_breakers'\n   ```\n   - Are limits too low for observed traffic?\n   - Are limits appropriate for upstream capacity?\n\n3. **Monitor connections and requests**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_active|upstream_rq_active|upstream_rq_pending\"\n   ```\n   - Are active connections at or near circuit breaker limit?\n   - Is pending queue building up?\n\n4. **Check upstream health**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters | grep your_cluster -A30\n   ```\n   - Are all hosts healthy?\n   - Are response times reasonable?\n   - Are there connection failures?\n\n5. **Review logs** for clues:\n   ```bash\n   grep -E \"overflow|reset|fail|goaway|timeout\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n### Best Practices\n\n1. **Set appropriate circuit breaker limits**:\n   - Measure peak values in production\n   - Set limits to 1.5-2x peak observed\n   - Use per-host limits to distribute load evenly\n\n2. **Monitor pool metrics continuously**:\n   - Alert on `*_overflow` metrics\n   - Alert on `upstream_cx_connect_fail` increasing\n   - Watch for unusual `upstream_rq_pending_active` values\n\n3. **Use multiple priorities** for critical traffic:\n   - Reserve capacity for HIGH priority traffic\n   - Prevent non-critical traffic from exhausting pools\n\n4. **Configure health checks** to detect unhealthy hosts:\n   - Remove unhealthy hosts before pools exhaust\n   - Rebalance traffic to healthy hosts\n\n5. **Tune timeouts appropriately**:\n   - `connect_timeout`: Set based on upstream distance/performance\n   - `request_timeout`: Set to ~2-3x typical request latency\n   - `idle_timeout`: Set to slightly larger than upstream timeout\n\n6. **Use preconnection** for latency-sensitive traffic:\n   - Reduce connection establishment latency\n   - Smooth out traffic spikes\n\n7. **Monitor upstream independently**:\n   - Ensure upstream isn't the bottleneck\n   - Monitor upstream resource usage (CPU, memory, connections)\n   - Validate upstream is not forcing connection resets\n\n8. **Test circuit breaker limits**:\n   - Load test with expected peak traffic\n   - Verify no `*_overflow` metrics occur\n   - Identify capacity constraints early\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":316,"cache_read_input_tokens":57172,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":316},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"8bc336fc-9d31-481a-a289-d3f657350e66","uuid":"537f4c76-b275-4668-8b96-58cef1bbf874"}

Architecture Overview\n\n### Connection Pool Organization\n\nEnvoy's connection pools are the critical infrastructure layer managing upstream connections. Understanding their architecture is essential for diagnosing production issues.\n\n#### Pool Hierarchy\n\n- **Per-Cluster Pools**: Each upstream cluster has its own pool manager\n- **Per-Host Pools**: Within each cluster, a separate connection pool exists for each upstream host\n- **Per-Thread Pools**: Connection pools are NOT shared across worker threads—each thread maintains its own independent pools\n- **Per-Priority Pools**: Separate capacity tracking for DEFAULT and HIGH priority streams (separate circuit breaker limits)\n\n#### Connection State Machine\n\nEach connection progresses through well-defined states:\n\n```\nConnecting → Ready/ReadyForEarlyData → Busy → Draining → Closed\n```\n\n**State Definitions:**\n\n- **Connecting**: Connection is being established, not yet available for requests\n  - File: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:90`\n  - Timer active: `connect_timeout` (default varies by cluster)\n\n- **Ready**: Connection is established, has capacity for additional concurrent streams\n  - HTTP/2: Has unused concurrent stream slots\n  - HTTP/1.1: Only one stream active at a time\n  - Transitions to Busy when capacity is exhausted\n\n- **ReadyForEarlyData** (HTTP/3 only): Connection established but handshake in progress\n  - Can accept requests before full TLS handshake\n  - Transitions to Ready or Busy on handshake completion\n\n- **Busy**: Connection is at its concurrent stream limit\n  - No new streams can be attached\n  - Pending requests queue and wait for capacity\n  - Transitions to Ready when a stream completes\n  - File: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:256-258`\n\n- **Draining**: No new streams will be assigned; connection closes after active streams complete\n  - Triggered by:\n    - HTTP/2 GOAWAY from peer\n    - Connection reaching `max_requests_per_connection` limit\n    - Administrative drain command\n  - File: `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`\n\n- **Closed**: Connection is no longer usable, queued for destruction\n  - Scheduled for deferred deletion\n  - All stream state has been released\n\n#### Internal Tracking Structures\n\nThe pool maintains several lists:\n\n```cpp\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> ready_clients_;              // Connections in Ready state\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> busy_clients_;               // Connections in Busy state\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> connecting_clients_;         // Connections in Connecting state\nstd::list<ActiveClientPtr> early_data_clients_;         // Connections in ReadyForEarlyData state\nstd::list<PendingStreamPtr> pending_streams_;           // Queued requests waiting for connections\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:300+`\n\n#### Capacity Tracking\n\nThe pool tracks available stream capacity across all connections:\n\n- `connecting_stream_capacity_`: Potential capacity from in-flight connections\n- `connecting_and_connected_stream_capacity_`: Total potential capacity (connecting + ready + busy)\n- `num_active_streams_`: Currently active request streams\n\nThese values are critical for:\n- Determining if new requests should be queued or rejected\n- Deciding whether to preconnect\n- Enforcing circuit breaker limits\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:26-50`\n\n### HTTP Protocol Differences\n\n#### HTTP/1.1 Pools\n- **Max concurrent streams per connection**: 1 (strictly enforced)\n- **Connection lifecycle**: Long-lived or short-lived based on `keep-alive`\n- **Queue behavior**: Pending requests queue when all connections are at capacity\n- **File**: `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.cc`\n\n#### HTTP/2 Pools\n- **Max concurrent streams per connection**: Configurable, negotiated via SETTINGS frame\n- **Default limit**: 2^29 (effectively unlimited in most cases)\n- **SETTINGS negotiation**: Server can lower max streams dynamically\n- **Stream multiplexing**: Multiple requests share one TCP connection\n- **Handling GOAWAY**: Transitions connection to Draining state, opens new connections for pending requests\n- **File**: `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.cc`\n\n#### HTTP/3 Pools (QUIC)\n- **Early data**: Requests can be sent before TLS handshake completes (0-RTT)\n- **State**: ReadyForEarlyData is unique to HTTP/3\n- **Connection migration**: Supported by QUIC (not managed by connection pool)\n- **File**: `source/common/http/http3/conn_pool.cc`\n\n---\n\n## 2. Common Failure Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Connection Pool Exhaustion — Pending Requests Overflow\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Upstream requests fail with `PoolFailureReason::Overflow`\n- Admin API shows non-zero `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` metric\n- Client observes 503 responses or request timeouts\n- Logs contain: `\"max pending streams overflow\"` or `\"max pending requests overflow\"`\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe pending request queue has hit the circuit breaker limit. When a new request arrives and there are no ready connections to serve it, the pool attempts to queue it as a pending request. However, the circuit breaker enforces `max_pending_requests` limit per priority level, and additional requests are rejected.\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()\n  → resourceManager(priority_).pendingRequests().canCreate()  [FAILS]\n  → onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason::Overflow)\n  → upstream_rq_pending_overflow_.inc()\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:347-352`\n\n**Why It Happens**:\n1. All connections in the pool are in Busy state (at concurrent stream limit)\n2. New connections are not being created fast enough\n3. Pending request backlog grows, hits `max_pending_requests` limit (default 1024)\n4. Circuit breaker rejects further pending requests\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Check pool statistics via admin API**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -A5 \"upstream_rq_pending\"\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -A5 \"upstream_cx\"\n   ```\n\n   Key metrics:\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_active`: Current pending request count\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_overflow`: Total overflow rejections\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_total`: Cumulative pending requests processed\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_total`: Total connections created\n   - `cluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_active`: Currently active connections\n\n2. **Examine cluster configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.@type | contains(\"Cluster\")) | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\")'\n   ```\n\n   Look for:\n   - `circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_pending_requests`\n   - `circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_connections`\n   - `circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_requests`\n\n3. **Check Envoy logs for connection creation patterns**:\n   ```bash\n   # Enable trace logging for connection pool\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?pool=trace\n\n   # Look for patterns in logs\n   grep \"queueing stream\\|using existing\\|creating new connection\\|max pending\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n4. **Analyze upstream health**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters | grep your_cluster -A20\n   ```\n   - Are all hosts up? If hosts are down or slow, connection creation fails\n   - Check `cx_total`, `rq_total`, and response times\n\n5. **Review request patterns**:\n   - Are requests slower than expected?\n   - Is the arrival rate higher than normal?\n   - Are requests getting retried (increasing pending queue)?\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Increase `max_pending_requests`** (short-term):\n   ```yaml\n   cluster_managers:\n     cluster:\n       name: your_cluster\n       circuit_breakers:\n         thresholds:\n         - priority: DEFAULT\n           max_pending_requests: 2048  # Increase from default 1024\n   ```\n   **Caveat**: This masks the root cause; investigate why pending backlog grows\n\n2. **Increase `max_connections`** to handle more concurrent work:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 2048  # Increase from default 1024\n   ```\n\n3. **Increase `max_requests`** per priority:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_requests: 2048  # Increase from default 1024\n   ```\n\n4. **Improve upstream responsiveness** (long-term):\n   - Optimize upstream service latency\n   - Add upstream capacity (more instances/hosts)\n   - Configure connection pooling on upstream side\n   - Enable request pipelining (HTTP/2 multiplexing)\n\n5. **Lower request timeout** if acceptable:\n   - Prevents slow requests from holding connections\n   - Frees capacity sooner for other requests\n\n**Code References**:\n- Pool overflow check: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:347`\n- Pending overflow metric: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:351`\n- Resource manager (circuit breaker enforcement): `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.cc`\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 2: Upstream Connection Reset or Premature Close\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Sporadic `LocalClose` or `RemoteClose` events in logs\n- Non-zero `upstream_cx_connect_fail` or `upstream_cx_reset` metrics\n- Requests fail mid-stream or don't reach upstream at all\n- Error messages: `\"upstream connection reset\"`, `\"connection refused\"`\n- `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` increases (pending requests fail)\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe upstream server is actively closing connections before streams complete. This can be due to:\n1. Upstream resource exhaustion (out of memory, CPU spike)\n2. Upstream graceful shutdown (sending GOAWAY or closing connections)\n3. Network issues (packet loss, timeout)\n4. Upstream load balancer killing idle connections\n5. Firewall/NAT timeout closing long-lived connections\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nNetwork::ConnectionCallbacks::onEvent(ConnectionEvent::RemoteClose)\n  → ConnPoolImplBase::onConnectionEvent()\n  → [If active streams exist]\n    → onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason::RemoteReset)\n    → upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject_.inc()\n  → [If idle, just clean up]\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:552-670`\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Isolate the failure pattern**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_reset|upstream_cx_destroy|upstream_cx_connect_fail\"\n   ```\n\n   - `upstream_cx_reset`: Unexpected disconnects\n   - `upstream_cx_connect_fail`: Connection failures during establishment\n   - `upstream_cx_destroy_local`: Local side closed (normal, drained)\n   - `upstream_cx_destroy_remote`: Remote side closed (abnormal)\n\n2. **Check per-host statistics**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters/your_cluster/stats\n   ```\n   - Are failures concentrated on one host? (indicates that host is unhealthy)\n   - Are they evenly distributed? (indicates network or upstream cluster issue)\n\n3. **Review Envoy logs for connection events**:\n   ```bash\n   # Enable debug logging\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?pool=debug\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?connection=debug\n\n   # Search for close events\n   grep \"ConnectionEvent::\\|RemoteClose\\|LocalClose\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n4. **Check upstream service health**:\n   ```bash\n   # Monitor upstream response times\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_rq_time_bucket|upstream_rq_pending_active\"\n\n   # Check if upstream is slow or unresponsive\n   # Look for increasing request latency\n   ```\n\n5. **Examine access logs for failed requests**:\n   ```bash\n   # Look for upstream_transport_failure_reason\n   grep \"upstream_transport_failure_reason\" access.log\n   grep \"upstream_connection_failure\" access.log\n   ```\n\n6. **Test connectivity to upstream**:\n   ```bash\n   # From Envoy pod/container:\n   telnet upstream-host upstream-port\n   timeout 5 bash -c 'cat < /dev/null > /dev/tcp/upstream-host/port'\n   ```\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Increase `connect_timeout`** if connections are dropping during establishment:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster:\n     name: your_cluster\n     connect_timeout: 5s  # Increase from default 1s\n   ```\n\n2. **Configure `tcp_keepalive`** to detect dead connections:\n   ```yaml\n   upstream_connection_options:\n     tcp_keepalive:\n       keepalive_probes: 3\n       keepalive_interval: 10s\n       keepalive_time: 30s\n   ```\n\n3. **Enable health checking** to detect unhealthy hosts:\n   ```yaml\n   health_checks:\n   - timeout: 1s\n     interval: 10s\n     unhealthy_threshold: 3\n     healthy_threshold: 2\n     http_health_check:\n       path: /health\n   ```\n\n4. **Set `idle_timeout`** to proactively close and recreate idle connections:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster_connection_draining:\n     idle_timeout: 300s\n   ```\n\n5. **Increase `max_requests_per_connection`** (HTTP/1.1) to reduce connection recycling:\n   ```yaml\n   http_protocol_options:\n     max_requests_per_connection: 10000\n   ```\n\n6. **Add connection draining grace period**:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster:\n     drain_connections_on_host_removal: true\n   ```\n\n**Fix - Operational/Upstream Changes**:\n- Optimize upstream service to handle load better\n- Add more upstream capacity\n- Review upstream garbage collection and resource limits\n- Ensure upstream keep-alive settings match Envoy expectations\n- Disable aggressive TCP timeouts on load balancers\n\n**Code References**:\n- Connection event handler: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:552`\n- Remote close handling: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:555-585`\n- TCP connection creation: `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc:14-35`\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 3: Circuit Breaker Triggering Unexpectedly\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Admin stats show `upstream_cx_overflow` or `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` increasing\n- All requests to a cluster start failing with \"overflow\" error\n- No actual errors on upstream; capacity appears available\n- Happens suddenly after a spike in traffic\n- Request errors after other clusters' traffic spikes\n\n**Root Cause**:\nCircuit breaker limits are being hit even though the upstream appears healthy. Common causes:\n1. **Shared circuit breaker limits**: Multiple clusters or priorities share resource manager\n2. **Capacity miscalculation**: `max_connections` or `max_pending_requests` set too low for actual concurrency\n3. **Slow response times**: Connections held longer, capacity exhausted sooner\n4. **Uneven load distribution**: Load balancer concentrating traffic on few hosts\n5. **Rate limiting**: Upstream rate limiting causes queue buildup\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nConnPoolImplBase::tryCreateNewConnection()\n  → host_->canCreateConnection(priority_)  [Circuit breaker check]\n  → [If exceeded]: upstream_cx_overflow_.inc()\n  → return ConnectionResult::NoConnectionRateLimited\n\nOR\n\nConnPoolImplBase::newStreamImpl()\n  → resourceManager(priority_).pendingRequests().canCreate()\n  → [If exceeded]: upstream_rq_pending_overflow_.inc()\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:198-202`, `347-352`\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Check circuit breaker limits vs actual load**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.@type | contains(\"Cluster\")) | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\") | .cluster.circuit_breakers'\n   ```\n\n   Compare configured limits with:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_active|upstream_rq_active|upstream_rq_pending_active\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Check for cascading failures**:\n   ```bash\n   # Get stats for multiple clusters\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_overflow|upstream_rq_pending_overflow\"\n\n   # If multiple clusters overflow at same time, check cluster manager limits\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"cluster_manager\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Review request latency**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"upstream_rq_time\"\n\n   # If latencies are high, connections are held longer\n   # Check if upstream is slow\n   ```\n\n4. **Examine resource manager state**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -A3 \"cluster.your_cluster.resource_manager\"\n   ```\n\n5. **Check priority-based limits**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"circuit_breakers\"\n   ```\n   - DEFAULT priority requests may be exhausted\n   - HIGH priority may have separate limits\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Adjust `max_connections` based on realistic concurrency**:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 4096  # Increase based on observed peak\n   ```\n\n2. **Adjust `max_requests` based on actual concurrent streams**:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_requests: 4096\n   ```\n\n3. **Use per-host limits** to distribute load more fairly:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 512\n     per_host_thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 50  # Limit per individual host\n   ```\n\n4. **Set separate limits for HIGH priority**:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_requests: 4096\n     - priority: HIGH\n       max_requests: 512  # Reserve capacity for critical traffic\n   ```\n\n5. **Monitor and increase limits based on metrics**:\n   - Set `track_remaining: true` to expose remaining capacity\n   - Create alerts on `circuit_breakers.*.remaining` metrics\n   - Incrementally increase limits based on observed peak\n\n**Code References**:\n- Circuit breaker enforcement: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:198-202`\n- Resource manager (limits enforcement): `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.h`\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 4: HTTP/2 GOAWAY Causing Request Failures\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Sporadic request failures after sustained traffic\n- Logs contain `\"remote goaway\"` messages\n- Admin stats show `upstream_cx_close_notify` incrementing\n- Multiple connection resets immediately after GOAWAY\n- Cascading failures as pending requests fail\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe upstream HTTP/2 server sent a GOAWAY frame, signaling that it will not accept new streams on this connection. Envoy must:\n1. Stop sending new streams to this connection\n2. Drain existing streams\n3. Open new connections for pending/future requests\n4. If upstream is not opening new connections, pending requests accumulate and fail\n\nGOAWAY can be initiated by:\n- Upstream graceful shutdown\n- Upstream resource exhaustion\n- Upstream hitting stream/connection limits\n- Upstream configured to close connections periodically\n- Load balancer injecting connection resets\n\n**Code Path**:\n```\nHttp::MultiplexedActiveClientBase::onGoAway()\n  → upstream_cx_close_notify_.inc()\n  → [If state != Draining]:\n    → [If no active streams]: close()\n    → [Else]: transitionActiveClientState(Draining)\n  → scheduleOnUpstreamReady()  [Attach pending streams to new connections]\n```\n\nFile: `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. **Confirm GOAWAY events**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_close_notify\n   ```\n   - Non-zero value indicates GOAWAY was received\n   - Increasing value indicates repeated GOAWAY events\n\n2. **Check connection state transitions**:\n   ```bash\n   # Enable trace logging\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?http=trace\n   POST localhost:9901/logging?pool=debug\n\n   grep -E \"remote goaway|transitionActiveClientState.*Draining\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n3. **Examine request failure patterns**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep \"upstream_rq_reset\\|upstream_rq_failed\"\n\n   # Correlate with GOAWAY events in timestamps\n   ```\n\n4. **Check if upstream can accept new connections**:\n   ```bash\n   # From Envoy:\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters/your_cluster | grep cx_\n\n   # Look for:\n   # - Increasing cx_total (new connections opened after GOAWAY)\n   # - Stuck cx_active (connections not draining)\n   ```\n\n5. **Review upstream logs**:\n   - Is upstream gracefully shutting down?\n   - Are connection limits being hit?\n   - Are resource limits triggering shutdown?\n\n**Fix - Configuration Changes**:\n\n1. **Increase `max_requests_per_connection`** to reduce GOAWAY frequency:\n   ```yaml\n   http_protocol_options:\n     max_requests_per_connection: 100000  # Increase from default (often 1024)\n   ```\n\n2. **Enable preconnection** to have connections ready when GOAWAY occurs:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster:\n     name: your_cluster\n     preconnect_policy:\n       per_upstream_preconnect_ratio: 1.5  # Open 150% of needed connections\n   ```\n\n3. **Increase connection pool size** to absorb GOAWAY events:\n   ```yaml\n   circuit_breakers:\n     thresholds:\n     - priority: DEFAULT\n       max_connections: 8192\n   ```\n\n4. **Configure read buffer limits** to prevent buffer exhaustion during GOAWAY:\n   ```yaml\n   http_protocol_options:\n     per_connection_buffer_limit_bytes: 32768\n   ```\n\n5. **Add connection draining timeout**:\n   ```yaml\n   cluster_connection_draining:\n     drain_timeout: 5s\n   ```\n\n**Fix - Operational/Upstream Changes**:\n- Review upstream connection/stream limits\n- Ensure upstream has enough capacity to handle load\n- Configure upstream to send GOAWAY less frequently (if possible)\n- Implement graceful shutdown with longer drain periods upstream\n- Use connection pooling on upstream side\n\n**Code References**:\n- GOAWAY handler: `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`\n- Connection draining: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:304-306`\n- Preconnect policy: `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:92-157`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Diagnostic Commands\n\n### Admin API Endpoints\n\n#### `/clusters` - Full Cluster Statistics\n\nProvides comprehensive statistics for all upstream clusters and hosts.\n\n**Command**:\n```bash\ncurl localhost:9901/clusters\n```\n\n**Output includes**:\n- `upstream_cx_total`: Total connections created\n- `upstream_cx_active`: Currently active connections\n- `upstream_cx_connect_fail`: Failed connection attempts\n- `upstream_cx_reset`: Connections reset by peer\n- `upstream_rq_total`: Total requests sent\n- `upstream_rq_active`: Currently in-flight requests\n- `upstream_rq_pending_total`: Total requests queued at pool\n- `upstream_rq_pending_active`: Currently queued requests\n- `upstream_rq_pending_overflow`: Rejected queued requests\n- `upstream_cx_overflow`: Rejected connection attempts (circuit breaker)\n- `upstream_cx_close_notify`: GOAWAY frames received (HTTP/2)\n- `upstream_cx_max_requests`: Connections reaching max request limit\n\n**Useful filters**:\n```bash\n# Check specific cluster\ncurl localhost:9901/clusters | grep -A50 \"your_cluster::\"\n\n# Get summary stats\ncurl localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream | head -30\n```\n\n#### `/stats` - Detailed Statistics\n\nProvides statistics in a flat, machine-readable format (text or JSON with admin extension).\n\n**Command**:\n```bash\n# Text format\ncurl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"cluster\\.\" | grep -E \"cx_|rq_\"\n\n# JSON format (if compiled with admin extension)\ncurl localhost:9901/stats?format=json | jq '.stats[] | select(.name | contains(\"upstream\"))'\n```\n\n**Key metrics for connection pool troubleshooting**:\n```\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_total                        # Total connections\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_active                       # Active connections\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_pending                      # Pending connections (Connecting state)\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_connect_fail                 # Connection failures\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_overflow                     # Circuit breaker rejections\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_close_notify                 # GOAWAY received\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_cx_max_requests                 # Max requests reached\n\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_total                        # Total requests\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_active                       # Active requests\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_total                # Total pending requests\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_active               # Currently pending\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_pending_overflow             # Pending overflow\ncluster.your_cluster.upstream_rq_time                         # Request latency histogram\n```\n\n#### `/config_dump` - Active Configuration\n\nShows the current running configuration (in protobuf JSON format).\n\n**Command**:\n```bash\n# Get cluster configuration\ncurl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.@type | contains(\"Cluster\"))'\n\n# Get specific cluster circuit breaker settings\ncurl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.@type | contains(\"Cluster\")) | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\") | .cluster.circuit_breakers'\n```\n\n**What to look for**:\n```json\n{\n  \"circuit_breakers\": {\n    \"thresholds\": [\n      {\n        \"priority\": \"DEFAULT\",\n        \"max_connections\": 1024,\n        \"max_pending_requests\": 1024,\n        \"max_requests\": 1024,\n        \"max_retries\": 3\n      }\n    ]\n  },\n  \"http_protocol_options\": {\n    \"max_requests_per_connection\": 2147483647\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Monitoring Connection Pool State\n\n**Watch pool statistics in real-time**:\n```bash\nwatch -n 1 'curl -s localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_active|upstream_rq_active|upstream_rq_pending\"'\n```\n\n**Monitor for failures**:\n```bash\nwatch -n 1 'curl -s localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"overflow|reset|fail|close_notify\"'\n```\n\n### Key Metrics Reference\n\n| Metric | Type | Meaning | Critical When |\n|--------|------|---------|-----------------|\n| `upstream_cx_total` | Counter | Total connections created | Should be increasing with traffic |\n| `upstream_cx_active` | Gauge | Currently open connections | Compare to `max_connections` limit |\n| `upstream_cx_overflow` | Counter | Connection creation rejected (circuit breaker) | Non-zero = circuit breaker triggered |\n| `upstream_cx_connect_fail` | Counter | Failed connection attempts | Non-zero = upstream unreachable |\n| `upstream_cx_reset` | Counter | Connections reset by peer | Indicates upstream instability |\n| `upstream_cx_close_notify` | Counter | GOAWAY frames received | (HTTP/2 only) upstream closing connections |\n| `upstream_cx_max_requests` | Counter | Connections reaching max request limit | Indicates churn, tune `max_requests_per_connection` |\n| `upstream_rq_total` | Counter | Total requests sent upstream | Should track with traffic |\n| `upstream_rq_active` | Gauge | Currently in-flight requests | Compare to `max_requests` limit |\n| `upstream_rq_pending_active` | Gauge | Requests queued in pool | Non-zero = pool backpressure |\n| `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` | Counter | Pending requests rejected | Non-zero = requests dropped due to queue full |\n| `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` | Counter | Pending requests failed due to connection reset | Indicates upstream instability |\n| `upstream_rq_time` | Histogram | Request latency (ms) | High values = slow upstream |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Configuration Fixes and Tuning\n\n### Circuit Breaker Configuration\n\nCircuit breakers prevent resource exhaustion by enforcing hard limits on concurrent connections, requests, and pending requests.\n\n#### Default Limits\n\n```yaml\ncircuit_breakers:\n  thresholds:\n  - priority: DEFAULT\n    max_connections: 1024\n    max_pending_requests: 1024\n    max_requests: 1024\n    max_retries: 3\n```\n\n#### Tuning Strategy\n\n1. **Baseline**: Start with defaults\n2. **Measure**: Observe peak values of `upstream_cx_active`, `upstream_rq_active`, `upstream_rq_pending_active`\n3. **Calculate**: Set limits to 1.5-2x peak observed values\n4. **Monitor**: Watch for `*_overflow` metrics; increase if frequently triggered\n5. **Iterate**: Gradually tune based on production behavior\n\n#### Configuration Template\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  # Circuit breaker limits\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n    - priority: DEFAULT\n      # Maximum simultaneous connections to cluster\n      # Tune: Observe upstream_cx_active, set to ~1.5x peak\n      max_connections: 512\n\n      # Maximum pending requests in pool queue\n      # Tune: Observe upstream_rq_pending_active, set to ~1.5x peak\n      max_pending_requests: 512\n\n      # Maximum simultaneous requests\n      # Tune: Observe upstream_rq_active, set to ~1.5x peak\n      max_requests: 512\n\n      # Maximum retries in flight\n      # Increase if retry storms occur\n      max_retries: 3\n\n      # (Optional) Per-host limits to distribute load evenly\n      # Only max_connections is supported per-host\n      max_connection_pools: 256\n\n    # (Optional) Separate limits for HIGH priority traffic\n    - priority: HIGH\n      max_connections: 256\n      max_pending_requests: 256\n      max_requests: 256\n\n    # (Optional) Per-host limits\n    per_host_thresholds:\n    - priority: DEFAULT\n      max_connections: 64  # Limit per individual host\n```\n\n### HTTP Connection Pool Configuration\n\n#### HTTP/1.1 Pools\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: http1_cluster\n  protocol: HTTP\n\n  http_protocol_options:\n    # Max requests per connection before recycling\n    # Tune: Higher = fewer connections, lower = better isolation\n    max_requests_per_connection: 10000\n\n    # TCP keep-alive settings\n    upstream_connection_options:\n      tcp_keepalive:\n        keepalive_probes: 3\n        keepalive_interval: 10s\n        keepalive_time: 30s\n```\n\n#### HTTP/2 Pools\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: http2_cluster\n  protocol: HTTP2\n\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    # Max concurrent streams per connection\n    # Tune: Higher = better multiplexing, lower = more connections\n    max_concurrent_streams: 100\n\n    # Connection idleness timeout\n    # Tune: Higher = long-lived connections, lower = connection recycle\n    idle_timeout: 600s\n\n  # HTTP/2-specific settings\n  http_protocol_options:\n    # Keep-alive period to prevent proxy timeouts\n    idle_timeout: 600s\n```\n\n#### Connection Timeout Configuration\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  # Timeout for establishing upstream connection\n  # Tune: Increase if upstream is geographically distant or slow\n  connect_timeout: 5s  # Default: 1s\n```\n\n### Preconnection Policy\n\nPreconnection improves latency by opening connections before requests arrive.\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  preconnect_policy:\n    # Ratio of connections to open speculatively\n    # Example: 1.5 = open 1.5x as many connections as active requests\n    per_upstream_preconnect_ratio: 1.5\n```\n\n### Connection Draining Configuration\n\n```yaml\ncluster:\n  name: your_cluster\n\n  # Drain timeout when removing cluster\n  cluster_connection_draining:\n    drain_timeout: 5s\n\n  # Close connections when removing host from cluster\n  close_connections_on_host_removal: true\n```\n\n### Resource Manager (Global Limits)\n\nEnvoy has global limits that apply across all clusters. If multiple clusters compete for resources, global limits may be exceeded first.\n\nCheck global limits via admin API:\n\n```bash\ncurl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"cluster_manager|resource_manager\"\n```\n\nOverride via bootstrap config (requires restart):\n\n```yaml\nbootstrap:\n  overload_manager:\n    refresh_interval: 0.25s\n    actions:\n    - name: envoy.overload_actions.shrink_heap\n      triggers:\n      - name: envoy.resource_monitors.fixed_heap\n        scaled: true\n        trigger_threshold: 0.9\n\n    # Connection limits\n    resource_limits:\n    - name: rpc.downstream_rq_active\n      actions:\n      - name: envoy.load_shed_points.http_connection_manager_decode_headers\n        action: SCALE_TIMER_MIN_WAIT\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Summary and Best Practices\n\n### Quick Troubleshooting Checklist\n\n1. **Identify the failure**:\n   - Check `/stats` for `*_overflow`, `*_reset`, `*_fail`, `*_close_notify` metrics\n   - Look at timestamps to correlate with traffic spikes or changes\n\n2. **Check configuration**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/config_dump | jq '.configs[] | select(.cluster.name==\"your_cluster\") | .cluster.circuit_breakers'\n   ```\n   - Are limits too low for observed traffic?\n   - Are limits appropriate for upstream capacity?\n\n3. **Monitor connections and requests**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_cx_active|upstream_rq_active|upstream_rq_pending\"\n   ```\n   - Are active connections at or near circuit breaker limit?\n   - Is pending queue building up?\n\n4. **Check upstream health**:\n   ```bash\n   curl localhost:9901/clusters | grep your_cluster -A30\n   ```\n   - Are all hosts healthy?\n   - Are response times reasonable?\n   - Are there connection failures?\n\n5. **Review logs** for clues:\n   ```bash\n   grep -E \"overflow|reset|fail|goaway|timeout\" envoy.log\n   ```\n\n### Best Practices\n\n1. **Set appropriate circuit breaker limits**:\n   - Measure peak values in production\n   - Set limits to 1.5-2x peak observed\n   - Use per-host limits to distribute load evenly\n\n2. **Monitor pool metrics continuously**:\n   - Alert on `*_overflow` metrics\n   - Alert on `upstream_cx_connect_fail` increasing\n   - Watch for unusual `upstream_rq_pending_active` values\n\n3. **Use multiple priorities** for critical traffic:\n   - Reserve capacity for HIGH priority traffic\n   - Prevent non-critical traffic from exhausting pools\n\n4. **Configure health checks** to detect unhealthy hosts:\n   - Remove unhealthy hosts before pools exhaust\n   - Rebalance traffic to healthy hosts\n\n5. **Tune timeouts appropriately**:\n   - `connect_timeout`: Set based on upstream distance/performance\n   - `request_timeout`: Set to ~2-3x typical request latency\n   - `idle_timeout`: Set to slightly larger than upstream timeout\n\n6. **Use preconnection** for latency-sensitive traffic:\n   - Reduce connection establishment latency\n   - Smooth out traffic spikes\n\n7. **Monitor upstream independently**:\n   - Ensure upstream isn't the bottleneck\n   - Monitor upstream resource usage (CPU, memory, connections)\n   - Validate upstream is not forcing connection resets\n\n8. **Test circuit breaker limits**:\n   - Load test with expected peak traffic\n   - Verify no `*_overflow` metrics occur\n   - Identify capacity constraints early\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
